Post Title: 
 Misleading advertising?
				
Post Content: 
This place has advertised in gumtree:





			
				Relaxation and sensual lomi lomi full body massage. 

caring and friendly, let me help you relax 
exchange massage ok. 

certificate III in beauty and relaxation massage 

PRICES 
half hr - $55 
45 min - $75 
1 hour - $89 

BOOK LAYLA, MON - FRI. 

PH: 96546635 

ADDRESS - 178 COLLINS STREET, MELBOURNE 3000, LOWER GROUND LEVEL. 

state " THIS IS NOT A SEXUAL SERVICE'
			
		

The reference to "exchange massage" suggests that the client can massage the masseuse (presumably for an additional fee) and that the masseuse will be naked.  That is not what one would expect in a straight massage.

Other words in the advertisement such as "sensual" and "full body" also suggest something more than a straight massage.

Of course, the advertisement also specifies "this is not a sexual service", but that sort of disclaimer seems to be standard practise for advertisements for massage in gumtree, presumably required by gumtree.  Even providers that are known to give extras include that diusclaimer in their advertisements.

A similar advertisement for this establishment has appeared in Craigslist:





			
				FULL BODY SENSUAL RELAXATION MASSAGE BY THE LOVELY LAYLA.

20 YEAR OLD, BLONDE, AUSTRALIAN GIRL

LET ME LOOK AFTER YOU

1/2 HR - $55
45MIN - $75
1 HOUR - $89

MUTUAL EXCHANGE MASSAGE OK.

BOOK , LAYLA

MONDAY -TO- FRIDAY

96546635

ADDRESS - LOWER GROUND LEVEL 178 COLLINS STREET , MELBOURNE 3000.

NOT A SEXUAL SERVICE.
			
		

That advertisement is even more suggestive, with a description of the "lovely Layla", although it contains the same disclaimer about not being a "sexual service".

The expectations aroused by the advertisements, with their suggestive wording, appear to be entirely belied by the experiences posted on this thread, which describe an entirely straight massage.

So what is the consensus of opinion?  Is this place engaging in misleading advertising, designed to attract clients by arousing expectations that will not be fulfilled?  Is the "lovely Layla" agreeable to an "exchange massage" an entirely fictitious person?

I would also like to ask a semantic question.  I was under the impression that the wording "not a sexual service" meant that only hand relief was on offer, not oral or full service, and a purely straight massage was indicated by the wording "strictly non-sexual service".  What are your thoughts?
